## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the instantaneous population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and population P. Classical population dynamics provides numerous ODE models ranging from exponential and logistic growth to more complex density-dependent and time-varying models.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, constant per-capita rate)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth common in tumor/biological populations)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with flexible density dependence)
- Strong Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population threshold)
- Von Bertalanffy growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance model)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized growth curve)
- Time-varying logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * sin(c3 * t) * P (seasonal environmental forcing)
- Exponential with time-dependent rate: dP_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * P (accelerating or decelerating growth rate)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional power density dependence)
- Logistic with harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (constant effort harvesting)
- Weak Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) * (1 - c2 * P) (positive density dependence at low P)
- Delayed density dependence proxy: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * t * P (time as proxy for lagged effects)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (rational density dependence minus mortality)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear dependence on P (dP_dt proportional to P) → exponential/Malthusian regime indicating density-independent per-capita growth rate
- Quadratic P term (P² appearing with negative coefficient) → logistic-type density-dependent self-limitation due to intraspecific competition
- Cubic P term (P³ or P*(P-a)*(1-bP)) → Allee effect indicating critical population thresholds below which growth becomes negative
- Logarithmic coupling log(P) multiplied by P → Gompertz-type growth with asymmetric approach to carrying capacity
- Fractional power P**c with 0<c<1 → surface-area-limited growth (e.g., nutrient absorption proportional to surface area rather than volume)
- Sinusoidal time dependence multiplied by P → seasonal or periodic environmental forcing on growth rate
- Ratio of polynomials in P (e.g., P/(1+cP)) → saturating functional response or resource limitation following Michaelis-Menten-type kinetics
- Difference of power laws (c0*P^a - c1*P^b) → competing anabolic and catabolic processes with different scaling exponents
- Exponential decay in time multiplying growth term → transient environmental change or resource depletion over time
- Product of multiple linear factors in P → multiple equilibria in population dynamics (extinction, intermediate, and carrying capacity)
